Jamison Brereton

6 (240)
Agni
Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra G─Бthina
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
From its beginning, this hymn signals AgniтАЩs dual roles as priest and ritual fire and as fire on earth and fire among the gods. The first verse contains a sustained ┼Ыleс╣гa, a word, or in this case a gapped word, with a double sense. The gapped feminine noun is probably the juh┼л╠Б, the sacrificial ladle with which the butter offerings are poured in the fire. But she can also be the tongue of the poetтАФnot so incidentally, another meaning of the word juh┼л╠БтАФor even the speech of the poets. If one of the two latter, then dakс╣гiс╣З─Бv─Б╠Бс╣н can mean not or not only тАЬconveying to the rightтАЭ but also, as Geldner suggests, тАЬconveying the priestly giftтАЭ (dakс╣гiс╣З─Б) to the Hotar Agni. Similarly, in verse 2, the draft-horses are primarily the flames of Agni, but they can also be the priests of the sacrifices.
From verse 3 the poet launches into his principal theme: the position of Agni himself as the intermediary between gods and humans, himself a kind of divine ┼Ыleс╣гa, who is simultaneously a Hotar for humans and a Hotar for the gods. The references to Heaven and Earth (vss. 3, 4) or to the тАЬtwo world-halvesтАЭ (vss. 5, 10) point toward his role as intermediary between earth and heaven. Similarly, in verse 7 Agni appears as both the heavenly fire, the sun, and as the earthly fire of the sacrifice. Reflecting his double manifestation, the first line of this verse could mean that Agni shines either as the earthly fire тАЬto heavenтАЭ or as the sun тАЬfrom heaven.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDevout ministrants, who are to be inspired by prayer, bring forth (the ladle) destined for the worship of the gods, which is to be conveyed to the south (of the fire-altar), and which, charged with (sacrificial) food, pointed to the east, containing the oblation, and, filled with liquefied butter, proceeds to Agni.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O praise-poets, twisting around in your mind, lead forth the one [=the sacrificial ladle] who is turned toward the gods, as you serve the gods; conveying (offerings) toward the right, the prizewinning mare goes to the east, bringing the offering to Agni, (she who is) rich in ghee.

Griffith

URGED on by deep devotion, O ye singers, bring, pious ones, the God-approaching ladle.
Borne onward to the right it travels eastward, and, filled with oil, to Agni bears oblation.

Oldenberg

Bring forward, ye pious singers, stirred in your thoughts 1, (the ladle) which is turned towards the gods. Carrying (the sacrificial butter) from left to right 2 it turns eastward, rich in strength, bringing the offering to Agni, full of ghee.

Geldner

Mit eurem Denken euch aufschwingend, ihr Dichter, holet gottergeben den f├╝r die G├╢tter bestimmten Schmalzl├╢ffel her! Von rechts gebracht, gewinnbringend, geht der Schmalzl├╢ffel vorw├дrts, f├╝r Agni die Opferspende bringend.

Grassmann

O S├дnger streckt mit Andacht eifrig wirkend, ihr Frommen, vor den L├╢ffel f├╝r die G├╢tter; Zur Rechten fahrend geht er vor mit Labsal, mit Fett gef├╝llt, dem Agni Festtrunk bringend.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni, as soon as born, occupy both heaven and earth; for you, to whom sacrifice is to be offered, exceed in magnitude the firmament and the earth; may your seven-tongued fires be glorified.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You filled the two world-halves as you were born, and now you, o you who seek the first offerings, have surpassed
even the heaven and the earth by your greatness, o Agni. Let your
draft-horses with their seven tongues twist around.

Griffith

Thou at thy birth didst fill both earth and heaven, yea, Most Adorable, thou didst exceed them.
Even through the heaven’s and through the earth’s expanses let thy swift seventongued flames roll on, O Agni.

Oldenberg

When born thou hast filled the two worlds, nay thou hast even exceeded them, O friend of sacrifices 1. May, O Agni, thy seven-tongued horses 2 move along, by the greatness of heaven and earth 3.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe firmament and the earth and the adorable (gods) propitiate you their invoker, for the (completion of the) sacrifice, whenever the descendants of Manu, pious, and bearing oblations, glorify your radiant flame.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Descendants of Manu: vi┼Ыaс╕е m─Бnuс╣г─лс╕е = manoс╕е sambandhinyaс╕е praj─Бс╕е, people connected with Manu

Jamison Brereton

Heaven and Earth and the (gods) worthy of the sacrifice set you down as the Hotar for the house,
when the clans of the sons of Manu, serving the gods and bearing
pleasing oblations, summon your gleaming flame.

Griffith

Both Heaven and Earth and Gods who should be worshipped establish thee as Priest for every dwelling,
Whenever human families, God-devoted, bringing oblations; laud thy splendid lustre.

Oldenberg

Heaven and Earth the worshipful 1 establish thee as Hotri for the house, whenever the pious human tribes offering food magnify the bright light.

Geldner

Himmel und Erde und die opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter setzen dich zum Opferpriester f├╝r das Haus ein, wenn die menschlichen St├дmme gottergeben, eine Labung bereithaltend, deine helle Flamme anrufen.

Grassmann

Dich setzen ein der Himmel und die Erde, die hehren G├╢tter f├╝r das Haus zum Priester, So oft der Menschen gottergeb’ne St├дmme, mit Trank versehn, dein helles Licht verehren.

Elizarenkova

рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рдЕрдзрд┐рдХреЛрд╣рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд╛рдореНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдпрдзрдирдЩреНрдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реНрднреВрдореНрдпреЛрд░реНрдордзреНрдпреЗ рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдиреЗрдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдирд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗрд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпреЗрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдГрдЕрдЪрд▓рдГрд╕рдиреН рдЖрдирд┐рд╖рддреНрддрдГ рдирд┐рд╖рдгреНрдгреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рдЖрд╕реНрдХреЗрдЖрдХреНрд░рдордгрд╢реАрд▓реЗ рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА рд╕рдорд╛рдирдГрдПрдХрдГрд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдГ рдкрддрд┐рд░реНрдпрдпреЛрд╕реНрддреЗрд╕рдкрддреНрдиреНрдпреМ рдЕрдЬрд░реЗрдЬрд░рд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗ рдЕрдореГрддреЗ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрдирд╛рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддреЗ рд╕рдмрд░реНрджреБрдШреЗ рд╕рдмрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрдореНрд░реБрддрдореБрджрдХрдВ рддрд╕реНрдпрджреЛрдЧреНрдзреНрд░реНрдпреМ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ рдЙрд░реБрдЧрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдпрдкреГрдереБрдЧрдордирд╕реНрдп рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрд╕реНрддреБрддреЗрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдзреЗрдиреВрдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреМрднрд╡рддрдГ рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe great and adorable Agni is firm seated on his spacious throne between heaven and earth; and the powerful fellow-brides (of the sun), the imperishable uninjurable (heaven and earth) are the two milk-yielding cows of the wide-extending (Agni).тАЭ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рдЙрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдкрд░рд┐рдорд╛рдгрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдореЗрдВ (рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдГ) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд▓ (рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдиреЗ) рдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╣рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ) рдХрд╛рдордирд╛ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдФрд░ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЗ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдмреАрдЪ рдореЗрдВ (рдЖ, рдирд┐рд╖рддреНрддрдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ (рдЖрд╕реНрдХреНрд░реЗ) рдЬрд┐рдирдХрд╛ рдЖрдХреНрд░рдордг рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдо рд╕реЗ рдЪрд▓рдирд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡ (рдЕрдЬрд░реЗ) рдЬреЛ рдЬреАрд░реНрдг рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ рд░рд╣рд┐рдд (рдЕрдореГрдХреНрддреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░ рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЕрд╢реБрджреНрдз (рд╕рдмрд░реНрджреБрдШреЗ) рдПрдХ рд╕реЗ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреВрд░реЗ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рдЙрд░реБрдЧрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп) рдмрд╣реБрддреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЬреЛ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рдЙрд╕рдХреА (рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА) рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди рд╡рд╛ (рдзреЗрдиреВ) рджреЛ рдЧреМрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╣реИрдВ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡рд╣ рд╕рдмрдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреЛ рдпрд╣ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХ рджреАрдЦ рдкрдбрд╝рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣ рд╕рдмрд╕реЗ рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рдФрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдкрд░рд┐рдзрд┐ рдореЗрдВ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рд╡рд╕рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╕рдм рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рдХрд┐ рджрд┐рди-рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐ рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдЙрд╕ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рдиреЛ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпреЛ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддреНрд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ рдзреНрд░реБрд╡реЛ рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдиреЗ рд╣рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгреЛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдирд┐рд╖рддреНрддреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛рд╕реНрдХреНрд░реЗ рдЕрдЬрд░реЗ рдЕрдореГрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕рдмрд░реНрджреБрдШреЗ рдЙрд░реБрдЧрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА рдзреЗрдиреВрдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рд╕ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН) рдорд╣рддреНрд╡рдкрд░рд┐рдорд╛рдгрдГ (рд╕рдзрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ (рдзреНрд░реБрд╡рдГ) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрд▓рдГ (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рдирд┐рд╖рддреНрддрдГ) рдирд┐рд╖рдгреНрдгрдГ (рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ) рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛) (рдорд╛рд╣рд┐рдиреЗ) рдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдиреЗ (рд╣рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ) рдХрдордиреАрдпрдГ (рдЖрд╕реНрдХреНрд░реЗ) рдЖрдХреНрд░рдордгрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡реЗ (рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА) рд╕рдкрддреНрдиреА рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ (рдЕрдЬрд░реЗ) рдЬреАрд░реНрдгрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗ (рдЕрдореГрдХреНрддреЗ) рд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдердпрд╛рд╜рд╢реБрджреНрдзреЗ (рд╕рдмрд░реНрджреБрдШреЗ) рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд░рдгрдкреНрд░рдкреВрд░рд┐рдХреЗ (рдЙрд░реБрдЧрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп) рдмрд╣реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╕реНрдп (рдзреЗрдиреВ) рдзреЗрдиреБрд╡рддреНрдкрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХреЗ реерекрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпреЛрд╜рдпрдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХреЛ рджреГрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рд╕ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рд╕реНрд╡рдкрд░рд┐рдзреМ рдирд┐рд╡рд╕рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рднреВрдЧреЛрд▓рд╛рдиреНрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрддрд┐ рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕рдореНрднрд╡рддрд╕реНрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдиреАрдд реерекрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGreat, Agni, are the deeds of you the mighty one; you have spread abroad by your power the heaven and earth; you have been the messenger (of the gods); as soon as begotten you have become the leader of men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Great are the commandments of you who are great, o Agni. Through your will you extend throughout the two world-halves.
You became the messenger as you were born. You are the leader of the different peoples, o bull.

Griffith

Great are the deeds of thee, the Great, O Agni: thou by thy power hast spread out earth and heaven.
As soon as thou wast born thou wast an envoy, thou, Mighty One, was Leader of the people.

Oldenberg

Thy, the great (god’s) laws, O Agni, are great. Through the power of thy mind thou hast spread out the two worlds. Thou hast become a messenger at thy birth, thou, O bull, the leader of the tribes.

Geldner

Gro├Я bist du und gro├Я ist dein Walten, o Agni. Mit deiner Einsicht hast du beide Welten durchzogen. Eben geboren wardst du der Bote, du der F├╝hrer der V├╢lker, o Bulle.

Grassmann

Gross bist du Agni, gross sind deine Werke, mit deiner Kraft erf├╝lltest du die Welten; Als du geboren, wurdest du der Bote und F├╝hrer du, o Stier, der Menschenst├дmme.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen, Agni, you abide in the woods, consuming the waters at your plural asure, then your rays illuminate the heavens, and you shine like many former radiant dawns; the gods themselves commend (the brilliancy) of their praise-meriting invoker.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your shining rays shine here even to heaven; you become radiant along with the many far-radiant dawns,
when, o Agni, the gods marvel at your busy burning at will among the wood, (the burning) by the delightful Hotar.

Griffith

Even from the sky thy brilliant lights shone hither: still hast thou beamed through many a radiant morning,
That the Gods praised their joyous Herald’s labour eagerly burning, Agni, in the forests.

Oldenberg

1 Even from heaven thy shining lights have shone; thy splendour follows many resplendent dawns, when the gods, O Agni, praised the cheerful Hotri’s work 2 who eagerly burns in the forests 3.

Geldner

Bis zum Himmel leuchten deine Leuchten; den vielen ergl├дnzenden Morgenr├╢ten gl├дnzest du nach, w├дhrend deiner gierig in den H├╢lzern brennenden T├дtigkeit, des wohlredenden Hotri, die G├╢tter Beifall spenden, o Agni.

Grassmann

Vom Himmel her auch strahlen deine Lichter, du leuchtest nach den vielen lichten Morgen, Wenn du im Holz die S├дfte gierig aufzehrst und G├╢tter sich des lieben Priesters freuen.

Elizarenkova

рдЙрд░реМрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгреЗ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдпреЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдорджрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рджрд┐рд╡рдГрд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░реЛрдЪрдиреЗрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдиреЗ рдЖрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдКрдорд╛рдГ рдКрдорд╕рдЮреНрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд╛рдГ рдкрд┐рддрд░рдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рдпрдЬрддреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕реБрд╣рд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдЖрдпреЗрдорд┐рд░реЗ рдЖрдпрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ рд░рдереНрдпрдГрд░рдерд┐рдирдГ рддрд╡ рдпреЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╣реЗрдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреИрдГрд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГрд╕рд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рдЖрдпрд╛рд╣реАрддрд┐рдЙрддреНрддрд░рдпрд░реНрдЪрд╛ рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рд╡рд╛рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдкреВрд░рдгрд╛рдГ рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe deities who sport in the spacious (firmament); those who are in the luminous sphere of heaven; the adorable Umas, who come when worthily invoked; the horses, Agni, that are fit for your car.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The adorable ┼кmas: ┼лm─Бс╕е = ┼лmasaс╣Еjmak─Бс╕е pitaraс╕е santi, the ┼кmas are the pitara, called ┼кm─Б

Jamison Brereton

Whether (they be) the gods who rejoice in the broad midspace or those who are in the luminous realm of heaven,
or those who are helpers, easily invoked and belonging to the
sacrificeтАФtheir chariot horses guided themselves here, o AgniтАФ

Griffith

The Gods who take delight in air’s wide region, or those the dwellers in heaven’s realm of brightness,
Or those, the Holy, prompt to hear, our helpers, who, carborne, turn their horses hither, Agni—

Oldenberg

Whether it be the gods who rejoice in the wide air, or those who dwell in the heavenly light, or those who are helpful 1, ready to hear our call, and worshipful; or whether the horses of thy chariot, O Agni, have turned themselves hitherтАФ

Geldner

Seien es die G├╢tter, die im weiten Luftraum schwelgen oder die im Lichtraum des Himmels sind oder welche verehrungsw├╝rdigen Helfer sonst sich gern rufen lassen, oder deren Wagenrosse, o Agni, hergelenkt wurden.

Grassmann

Die G├╢tter, die in weiter Luft sich freuen, und die im hellen Licht des Himmels weilen, Und die erh├╢rend, hold verehrungsw├╝rdig, des Wagens Stuten, Agni, herw├дrts lenkten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith all these in one chariot, Agni, or in many (chariots), come to our presence, for your horses are able; bring the three and thirty divinities with their wives, for the sake of (the sacrificial) food, and exhilarate them (all with the Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The three and thirty divinities with their wives: patn─лvatas triс╣Г┼Ыatam tr─лс╣Г┼Ыca dev─Бn: the first is, literally, having wives, but sometimes considered a proper name

Jamison Brereton

With these, o Agni, journey here near to us on the same chariot, or on a different chariot, for your horses are wide-ranging.
Convey here the three and thirty gods along with their wives, in
accordance with your own will; make then rejoice!.

Griffith

With these, borne on one ear, Agni, approach us, or borne on many, for thy steeds are able.
Bring, with their Dames, the Gods, the Three and-Thirty, after thy Godlike nature, and be joyful.

Oldenberg

Come hither with them, O Agni, on one chariot or on many chariots, for thy horses are powerful. Bring hither, after thy nature, the thirty and the three gods with their wives, and rejoice (in the Soma).

Geldner

Mit denen komm heran, o Agni, auf gleichem Wagen oder auf besondrem Wagen, denn du hast ausreichend Rosse. Die dreiunddrei├Яig G├╢tter mit ihren Frauen fahre aus eigener Vollmacht her und erg├╢tze dich!

Grassmann

Mit denen Agni komm auf gleichem oder verschiednen Wagen, stark sind ja die Rosse; Die drei und dreissig G├╢tter nebst den Frauen, die fahre her freiwillig und berausch dich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe is the invoker (of the gods), whom the spacious heaven and earth glorify, for the sake of increase, at repeated sacrifices; charged with water, they await like holy rites, propitious to the real presence of him who is born of truth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He is the Hotar, whose every sacrifice even the two broad world-halves welcome in order to make it strong.
Turned eastward like two rites stand the two well-supported
(world-halves), the two truth-possessing (parents) of truth-begotten (Agni), the two real ones.

Griffith

He is the Priest at whose repeated worship even wide Heaven and Earth sing out for increase.
They fair and true and holy coming forward stand at his sacrifice who springs from Order.

Oldenberg

He is the Hotri whose sacrifice even the two wide worlds salute over and over again for the sake of prosperity. Turned to the east 1, the two well-established 2 (goddesses, Heaven and Earth), the righteous, true ones stand as at the sacrifice 3 of (Agni) the right-born.

Geldner

Er ist der Hotri, dessen Opfer auch die beiden weiten Welten immer wieder zustimmen, da├Я es gedeihlich werde. Beide stehen bereit da wie das Opfer, ihren Platz behauptend, die rechtzeitigen, wahrhaftigen M├╝tter des zu rechter Zeit geborenen Agni.

Grassmann

Er ist der Priester, dessen Opfer alle zum Heil geniessen, selbst die weiten Welten; Voran beim Opfer standen sch├╢n sie tr├дufelnd, die reinen, wahren, reinem Werk entsprossen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGrant, Agni, to the offerer of the oblation, the earth, the bestower of cattle, the means of many (pious rites); such that it may be perpetual; may there be to us sons and grandsons born in our race, and may our good-will ever be upon us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

End of the second aс╣гс╣нaka

Jamison Brereton

тАУ Make the milk-libation, the very wondrous winning of the cow, succeed, o Agni, for him who invokes you most constantly.
There should be for us a son and a lineage that proliferates. Agni, let this your favor be for us.

Griffith

As holy food, Agni, to thine invoker give wealth in cattle, lasting, rich in marvels.
To us be born a son and spreading offspring. Agni, be this thy gracious will to usward.

Oldenberg

11 = III, 1, 23.

Geldner

Erziel, o Agni, Segen, den vielwirkenden Lohn einer Kuh f├╝r den am h├дufigsten rufenden S├дnger! Ein leiblicher Sohn, der das Geschlecht fortpflanzt, soll uns werden. Agni, diese Gnade von dir soll uns zuteil werden!

Grassmann

Dem Beter schaff als Labung wunderreichen Besitz an Rindern fort und fort, o Agni, Ein eigner Sohn sei uns und Stammvermehrung, das sei uns, Agni, deine Gunsterweisung.

Elizarenkova

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддрдореЗрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрд│рд╛рдореН) рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рд╛рдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рдкреБрд░реБрджрдВрд╕рдореН) рдмрд╣реБрдХрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рд╕рдирд┐рдореН) рд╡рд┐рднрдХреНрддрдореН (рдЧреЛрдГ) рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╢рд╢реНрд╡рддреНрддрдордореН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрдирд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рднреВрддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдореН (рд╣рд╡рдорд╛рдирд╛рдп) рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрджреНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп (рд╕рд╛рдз) рд╕рд╛рдзреНрдиреБрд╣рд┐ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╕реВрдиреБрдГ) (рддрдирдпрдГ) (рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╛) (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) (рд╕рд╛) (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рд╕реБрдорддрд┐рдГ) (рднреВрддреБ) (рдЕрд╕реНрдореЗ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рд╕реБ реерезрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрджрд┐ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджреЗрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдп рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рдпреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрд░рдВрд╕реНрддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рддреЗрд╖реБ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рдзрдирдзрд╛рдиреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рднрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд┐реерезрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджрдЧреНрдирд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреГрддреАрдпрдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдардВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧреЛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЗрд╜рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗрд╜рд╖реНрдЯрдореЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдорд╖реНрдЯрдХрдВ рдЪ рдкреВрд░реНрддрд┐рдордЧрд╛рддреН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд░ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рдЕрдЧреНрдиреА рд╡ рдкреГрдереНрд╡реА рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЬрд╛рдгреВрди рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдд рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХреЗрд▓реЗ рддрд░ рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░, рдкреМрддреНрд░, рдзрди, рдзрд╛рдиреНрдп, рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдИрд▓. рее резрез рее
